chmod -R o+rwx /home/ec2-user

/usr/lib64/mpich/bin/mpif90 /home/ec2-user/cohabit/program.f90 -ffree-line-length-none -o /home/ec2-user/cohabit/cox
/usr/lib64/mpich/bin/mpiexec -f /home/cluster/cohab/nodelist -np 4 /home/cluster/cohab/cox





/usr/lib64/mpich2/bin/mpif90 /home/agemici/checkobj/program.f90 -ffree-line-length-none -o /home/agemici/checkobj/coh

attach volume /dev/sdh at console first
    6  pwd
    7  cd dev
    8  dir
    9  mke2fs -F -j /dev/sdh
   10  mkdir /vol
   11  mount /dev/sdh /vol
   12  df -h
   13  nano /etc/fstab
   14  history
   15  yum install gcc48-gfortran.x86_64
   16  sudo yum install mpich-devel
   17  history
   18  pwd
   19  cd ..
   20  cd vol/
   21  dir
   22  mkdir cohabit
   23  cd ..
   24  cd cd vol
   25  cd vol
   26  dir
   27  cd cohabit/

upload files through winscp to /vol/

then login again 
chmod -R o+rwx /home/ec2-user    THIS ONE IS DANGEROUS! 
sudo su 
cp /home/ec2-user/cohabit/* /vol/cohabit/


groupadd data
useradd -G data cluster
su cluster
ssh-keygen -t dsa

cat ~/.ssh/id_dsa.pub >> ~/.ssh/authorized_keys
chmod 644 ~/.ssh/authorized_keys
exit


create images now 


In order to give permission to ec2-user:

d=0
do dm=1,Nthome
    do df=1,Nthome
        do hm=1,Ntwork
            do hf=1,Ntwork
                mydms(d)=dm
                mydfs(d)=df
                myhms(d)=hm
                myhfs(d)=hf
                d=d+1
            end do 
        end do 
    end do 
end do 
if (d .ne. (Nthome**2)*(Ntwork**2)) then
    print*, "Sometihing is so very wrong! ",d,(Nthome**2)*(Ntwork**2)
    stop
end if

mygroup2=mod(myid,NUMGROUPS)     ! which group each process belongs to: myid mygroup: 0 0 / 1 1 / 2 0 / 3 1 / 4 0 / 5 1 / 6 0 / 7 1 
mygrank2=int(myid/NUMGROUPS)     ! the rank of each process within their group: myid mygrank: 0 0 / 1 0 / 2 1 / 3 1 / 4 2 / 5 2 / 6 3 / 7 3 
mydm = mydms(mygrank2)
mydf = mydfs(mygrank2)
myhm = myhms(mygrank2)
myhf = myhfs(mygrank2)
call mpi_comm_split(mpi_comm_world,mygroup,mygrank,comm,mpierr)

121516
asked AWS SUPPORT ABOUT BEING ASKED FOR PASSWORD WHEN I TRY TO CHANGE FROM USER CLUSTER TO ROOT OR EC2-USER. I DID THE BELOW AND THE LOG OF THAT IS AFTER THIS MESSAGE FROM THEM. ALSO NOTE THAT I HAD TO DO CHMOD 600 CLOUD-INIT TO 
GIVE WRITE PERMISSION TO ROOT BEFORE I CHANGED THAT FILE. THAT IS NOT INCLUDED 
INT HE MESSAGE BELOW. 

Looking at the case logs, I understand that the newly created AMI have two user accounts (ec2-user and cluster) and you have trouble while switching between user accounts. You are being prompted for password. Please correct me if I have understood wrongly.

Based on the output you provided, I was able to understand that the instance is i-02b56ac8eb89079ed and is running with AMI - ami-f85c0590.
Being the original AMI is an Amazon AMI, I assume you access this instance with username as ec2-user and with SSH keypair file as key121416.pem. 

So whenever you login with ec2-user, you can gain root access by running the command 'sudo su'. By default, ec2-user is allowed in the sudoers list. But when you manually add any other users[1], you may have to add him to the sudoers file based on the requirement.
I believe this user 'cluster' is added manually and you might have missed to add him to the sudoer file.

As I see from your command output, whenever you run 'sudo su' or 'su ec2-user', it is prompting you for a password. This is because 'cluster' user is not in the sudoers list. 

I would recommend you to manually add the below entry to "/etc/sudoers.d/cloud-init" file. This would allow the user 'cluster' to perform the sudo without prompting for password.
cluster ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL

Once added, you can login with 'cluster' user and get root access by doing 'sudo su'. 
And if you want to switch from cluster to ec2-user user, you need to run command 'sudo su ec2-user' but not 'su ec2-user'.



[root@ip-10-0-0-153 etc]# cd sudoers.d/
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# vi cloud-init
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# 
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# 
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# sudo su
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# 
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# 
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# ls -al
total 12
drwxr-x---  2 root root 4096 Dec 15 08:31 .
drwxr-xr-x 74 root root 4096 Dec 14 17:28 ..
-r--r-----  1 root root  147 Dec 14 17:27 cloud-init
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# 
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# 
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# chmod 600 cloud-init
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# ls -al
total 12
drwxr-x---  2 root root 4096 Dec 15 08:31 .
drwxr-xr-x 74 root root 4096 Dec 14 17:28 ..
-rw-------  1 root root  147 Dec 14 17:27 cloud-init
[root@ip-10-0-0-153 sudoers.d]# vi cloud-init


THE CLOUD-INIT FILE LOOKS LIKE THE FOLLOWING:
ec2-user ALL = NOPASSWD: ALL

# User rules for ec2-user
ec2-user ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL

# User rules for ec2-user
ec2-user ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL

# User rules for cluster
cluster ALL=(ALL) NOPASSWD:ALL

compmig:

#!/bin/bash
## My first script

echo "Cat to combo and then compile to create executable called combo"

DIR1=/home/ec2-user/migit
DIR2=/vol/migit

#cp $DIR1/*     $DIR2/.
#cp $DIR1/agres.txt     $DIR2/.
#cp $DIR1/cohabinit.txt $DIR2/.
#cp $DIR1/cohabPSID.txt $DIR2/.
#cp familymigPSID.txt $DIR2/.
#cp bestpar121416.txt $DIR2/.

echo "I am here !"

echo "I am here 2!"

cd $DIR1

echo "I am here 3!"
cat nrtype.f90 nrutil.f90 nr.f90 pNelder_mead.f90 indexx.f90 sort2.f90 locate.f90 gauher.f90 alib.f90 mig_params.f90 mig_share.f90 mig_yaz.f90 mig_sol.f90 mig_mom.f90 mig_objf.f90 mig_main.f90 > $DIR1/program.f90

echo "I am here 4!"


/usr/lib64/mpich/bin/mpif90 $DIR1/program.f90 -ffree-line-length-none -fbounds-check -o $DIR1/mig.x

echo "Done"

copumig

!/bin/bash

echo "Copying files to all other nodes!"

for ITEM in mig.x familymigpsid.txt bestpar121416.txt

PNELDER_MEAD NOTES

IF YOU USE THE PNELDER_MEAD  FROM /TRAINING FILES/AUG16 FGL CODE FROM NOW ON
THE ONLY DIFFERENCE FROM THAT FILE IS THE FOLLOWING (IE. ADD USE NRTYPE AND COMMENT OUT INTEGER, PARAMETER :: DP= PART): 
MODULE pNelder_Mead
use nrtype
IMPLICIT NONE
INCLUDE 'mpif.h'
!INTEGER, PARAMETER :: dp = SELECTED_REAL_KIND(12, 60)
PRIVATE
PUBLIC :: pminim
AND ALSO WOULD NEED TO CHANGE THE DECLARATION OF THE ARGUMENTS OF THIS SUBROUTINE IN THE CALLING PROGRAM. BECAUSE THESE ARE REAL AND THE CALLING PROGRAM DECLARES THEM AS REAL(DP).

BUT WILL NOT USE PNELDER MEAD FROM TRAINING FILES/AUG16FGLCODE BECAUSE:

SEARCHED FOR PNELDER MEAD IN ALL MAILBOXES:
LOOK AT THE EMAIL I SENT TO STEVE ON 2/10/13 AND HIS REPLY 2/11/13 
FOR THE INFORMATION ON THINGS CHANGED ON PNELDER MEAD AROUND THAT TIME 
ON THE 2/11/13 EMAIL HE ALSO MENTIONS CORRECTING SOMETHING ABOUT MPI_REAL AND MPI_REAL8. THIS CORRECTION IS NOT IN THE PNELDER MEAD IN TRAINING FILES AUG16 FGL CODE DIRECTORY 
 
NOT SURE ABOUT THE OTHER PNELDER MEAD FILES THAT HAVE MORE EXPLANATIONS OF WHAT IS HAPPENING IN THE CODE ETC. (WILL HAVE TO DO A MORE THOROUGH COMPARISON OF 
PNELDER MEAD HOLD IN MIGIT, THE ONE IN COHABITC/CLUSTER_040615, THE ONE IN 
COHABIT/CODE_050313 O, AND MAYBE OTHERS. 

WILL USE THE PNELDER MEAD IN COHABITC/CLUSTER 040615
THIS HAS THE THERMOSTAT CORRECTION AS WELL AS MPI REAL8 (AMONG MORE EXPLANATIONS AND ALSO OVERALL USAGE OF REAL8. I DONÕT KNOW IF THAT LAST ONE (I.E. OVERALL USAGE OF REAL8) IS NECESSARY BUT ITÕS THERE AND I WILL USE IT LIKE THAT RATHER THAN THE VERSION WITH JUST REALÕS WHICH IS THE TRAINING FILES VERSION. USING REALS IN PNELDER WOULD REQUIRE ME TO CHANGE HTE DECLARATION OF ITS ARGUMENTS IN THE CALLING PROGRAM ANYWAY). 

DID HAVE TO MAKE SOME SLIGHT CHANGES TO COHABITC/CLUSTER 040615 VERSION TO BE ABLE TO 
USE IT IN MIGIT. SEE THE BEGINNING OF PNELDER IN MIGIT DIRECTORY TO SEE 
WHAT THESE SMALL CHANGES WERE. 

MORE INFO ABOUT THE DIFFERENCE BETWEEN THE TRAINING FILES PNELDER MEAD AND THE 
OTHER VERSIONS:

> !For example: if numprocs is 2 so that myrank is 0 or 1, we will 
> !have myimax=np1 for myrank=0 and myimax=np1-1 for myrank=1. 
> !Thes are the worst and the second worst points in the current simplex values with thermal fluctuations
> !   A reflection of the worst-response point W is performed and the response RR of the reflected point R is evaluated. 
> !	Reflect the worst (i.e.G(MYIMAX,:)) point through PBAR
> !	Call this reflection point PSTAR and evaluate the obj function at PSTAR
> !	HSTAR = function value at PSTAR
>  pstar = a * (pbar - g(myimax,:)) + pbar
>  CALL functn(pstar,hstar)
>  IF ((iprint > 0).AND.(realrank==0)) THEN
> 	WRITE (lout,*) 
> 	WRITE (lout,*) 
> 	WRITE (lout,'("REFLECTION --> reflecting MAXIMUM through PBAR to get the reflection point PSTAR. ")') 
> 	WRITE (lout,'("(R) PSTAR = a * (PBAR - g(imax,:)) + PBAR ")') 
> 	WRITE (lout,'("(RR) HSTAR=functn(PSTAR,HSTAR) ")') 
> 	WRITE (lout,*) 
>  END IF
> 
> 	! NOW EACH PROCESSOR DOES THE FOLLOWING SEPARATELY:
> 	! Each processor follows instrcutions based on hstar, returns a point MYPOINT with value MYVAL
> 	! in approproate index corresponding to which processor. Record what happened in entry of MYCASE
> 
> 	! case 1: hstar < hmin 
> 	! reflection did well i.e. hstar is beter than the best point hmin 
> 	! ---> expand further i.e. expand pbar in the direction of pstar
> 	! ---> g and h at expansion pt: PSTST,HSTST
> 	IF (hstar-thermstar(myrank+1) < htherm(1)) THEN ! case 1 - return the better of the expansion point and the reflection point
> 		mycase(myrank+1)=1
> 		pstst = c * (pstar - pbar) + pstar
> 		CALL functn(pstst,hstst)
> 		IF (hstst<hstar) THEN ! return expansion point (pstst)
> 			mypoint(myrank+1,:)=pstst
> 			myval(myrank+1)=hstst
> 		ELSE ! return reflection point (pstar)
> 			mypoint(myrank+1,:) = pstar
> 			myval(myrank+1) = hstar
> 		END IF
> 		
> 	! case 2: hstar > hmin  and hstar<htherm(np1-1) or (np1-2) ... (np1-myrank-1) .. etc. 	
> 	! reflection did ok i.e. hstar not beter than the best point, BUT better than the second (or third etc. depending on myrank) worst point 
> 	! ---> do nothing and just return the original reflection point pstar.  
> 	! ---> Note that this is the only case in which the processor does not do an extra function call
> 	ELSEIF (hstar-thermstar(myrank+1)<htherm(np1-myrank-1)) THEN ! case 2 - return the relction point
> 		mycase(myrank+1)=2
> 		mypoint(myrank+1,:)=pstar
> 		myval(myrank+1) = hstar
> 
> 	! case 3 or 4: hstar > hmin AND hstar > hterm(..) 
> 	! reflection did not do any good i.e. hstar not better than the best AND not better than any of the worst points
> 	! ---> contract by getting the convex combo of pstar and pbar
> 	! ---> contraction point: PSTST
> 	! ---> fnctn value at contraction point: HSTST
> 	ELSE 
> 		! calculate contraction point, pstst
> 		pstst= b * pstar + (one-b) * pbar
> 		CALL functn(pstst,hstst)
> 		! compare the contraction point to the better of pstar and the original point of the simplex
> 		IF (hstar-thermstar(myrank+1)<htherm(myimax)) THEN ! pstar is better of the two
> 			IF (hstst<hstar) THEN ! case 3 - return the contraction point
> 			mycase(myrank+1)=3
> 			mypoint(myrank+1,:)=pstst
> 			myval(myrank+1) = hstst
> 			ELSE ! case 4 - return the better of pstar and the original point, which is here pstar
> 			mycase(myrank+1)=4
> 			mypoint(myrank+1,:)=pstar
> 			myval(myrank+1) = hstar
> 			ENDIF
> 		ELSE ! ther original point of the simplex is better than pstar
> 			IF (hstst-thermstst(myrank+1)<htherm(myimax)) THEN ! case 3 - return the contraction point
> 			mycase(myrank+1)=3
> 			mypoint(myrank+1,:)=pstst
> 			myval(myrank+1) = hstst
> 			ELSE ! case 4 - return the better of pstar and the original point of the simplex,here g(myimax,:)
> 			mycase(myrank+1)=4
> 			mypoint(myrank+1,:)=g(myimax,:)
> 			myval(myrank+1) = h(myimax)

LENA INFO:
command lines to search for and then install gfortran: 
    yum search fortran
    yum install gcc48-gfortran.x86_64
    which gfortran
  

yum search gfortran
     searches online for where to download gfortran from
     for example, you would get the following output from this command line: 

[ec2-user@ip-10-0-0-107 migit]$ yum search gfortran
Loaded plugins: priorities, update-motd, upgrade-helper
=============================================================================== N/S matched: gfortran ===============================================================================
gcc-gfortran.noarch : Fortran support
gcc44-gfortran.x86_64 : Fortran support
gcc48-gfortran.x86_64 : Fortran support
libgfortran.i686 : Fortran runtime
libgfortran.x86_64 : Fortran runtime

Name and summary matches only, use "search all" for everything.




yum install gcc48-gfortran.x86_64 
	installs one of the above listed files (in this case the gcc48 one)


which gfortran
	when you run this command line, it tells you where the compiling and executing files for gfortran have been installed to 
       you need these directories because in linux, you canÕt just write ifort program.f90 -o mig.x, you have to TELL the computer what directory ifort is (in the intel case, I    	donÕt know what the compiling counterpart for gfortran is. for mpi case, itÕs mpif90 but I donÕt know remember the case without mpi. according to the following link, 
       it is just gfortran: https://gcc.gnu.org/wiki/GFortranGettingStarted)

for more on installing: 
https://gcc.gnu.org/wiki/InstallingGCC


when you run the Ôwhich gfortranÕ command line, you would get something like this: 
[ec2-user@ip-10-0-0-107 migit]$ which gfortran
/usr/bin/gfortran

so that means that you have to change that compmig file and replace 
   
/usr/lib64/mpich/bin/mpif90 $DIR1/program.f90 -ffree-line-length-none -fbounds-check -o $DIR1/mig.x


WITH

/usr/bin/gfortran $DIR1/program.f90 -ffree-line-length-none -fbounds-check -o $DIR1/mig.x

thatÕs why you do Ôwhich gfortranÕ (i.e. to figure out where that directory is)


once you have the executable file mig.x, then you can run that with the command line: 
./mig.x


(you must include the explicit path ./ of the executable's present directory as shown, when executing an executable. The Ò./Ò thing basically says Òthe mig.x in the current directoryÓ if you just use command line Òmig.xÓ, it would not be able to find that file unless your current directory is in the PATH)

note: in the above -fbounds-check is a compiler option that checks for whether there is any arrays going out of bounds situations (at run time check). 
the other compiler option is -fcheck=all which checks for everything. 
these compiler options slows down the runtime, so only use when not estimating. but do use them to check things every now and then especially when you change the code etc.
****************************************

121318: 

Just use the image from this month to launch instances spot or:

even if you don't use that image, the only thing you have to do is install fortran by:
yum search fortran 
sudo yum install gcc48-gfortran.x86_64 
sudo yum install mpich-devel

for the mpi when you do which mpicexec, (or maybe yum search mpich to install it in the first place), it says there isn't anything but it is there 
look in the relevant directory which you can see from the usual command
/usr/lib64/mpich/bin/mpiexec


make sure you launch the instance with HPC security group. otherwise you can't connect










122018:

before you start:
create a user trhough the IAM link in the AWS Console. 
this user comes with AWS access key id and secret access key etc. 

how to actually do it:
used various combinations of the below instructions to be able to install and use was parallel cluster:
https://aws.amazon.com/blogs/opensource/aws-parallelcluster/


the steps I followed (roughly):
first installed AWS cli (just google how to do it because I Don't know anymore)
then did:  pip install aws-parallelcluster
had problems with this installation because of something that has to do with pip or python or something. but eventually it worked after trying zillions of different things by using the following website: 
https://docs.python-guide.org/starting/install3/osx/#install3-osx 
if you have to do this again, you'll just have to do the trial and error thing because 
I don't know what did work eventually (I'll copy the log below either way). most of the problems I ran into had to do with the python version that was already installed in the mac. so I had to reinstall a newer version but then uninstall the older? and also changed the path? all those things are in the python guide website above. 



logging into the was parallel cluster (it doesn't include the last bit in the instructions above so I had to figure this out in the website pasted after the command below):
pcluster ssh hello-cluster1 -i "key121318.pem"
https://aws-parallelcluster.readthedocs.io/en/latest/commands.html#ssh


other pages that might have helped:
https://aws-parallelcluster.readthedocs.io/en/latest/getting_started.html
https://aws-parallelcluster.readthedocs.io/en/latest/configuration.html#layout

we examine how the introduction of microfinance affects the evolution ofsocial networks in villages in rural India. Social networks are an important source of credit,insurance, information, advice, and other economic and non-economic benefits.1 One wouldexpect that people who get microfinance loans would change their networks of informalborrowing and lending. What is interesting and perhaps less obvious, is that the thatexposure to microfinance induces widespread changes in social and economic networks, wellbeyond the people directly involved in microfinance borrowing and beyond relationships ofborrowing and lending. We argue, based on this evidence, that network formation exhibitsseveral key features: social effort is needed to maintain current relationships, forming newconnections involves significant chance in meetings (Òundirected searchÓ), and different typesof relationships are formed at the same time (multiplexing).

As more aspects of our life move to digital networks, crime comes with them. 
Our lives increasingly depend on the internet and digital networks, but these create new vulnerabilities and new ways for criminals to exploit the digital environment. 
Not only can many existing crimes be replicated in online environments, but novel crimes that exploit specific features of digital networks have emerged as well. 
With new crimes come new forms of policing and new forms of surveillance, and with these come new dangers for civil liberties. 

The shift to digital env alters our understanding of crime in five different ways. 
1. alert the scene or location where crimes occur. 
2. facilitates the commission fo new types of crimes. 
3. produces significant changes in law enforcement methods, for example, a shift to prevention and to new forms of cooperation between public and private actors.  e
4. gives law enforcement new tools of digital surveillance and net methods of sorting data and managing online risks. 
5. presents new challenges to the existing legal process and spurs the development of new forms of proof and procedure. 

the new crime scene - the digital networked environment. Online criminal behavior exploits the physical and social features of the internet. Five key features of the online world create new security risks and shape the kinds of criminal behavior we find there. 
1. digitalization- common standards for data transmission tha enable manipulation and modification. 
2. anonymity
3. interconnectivity 
4. decentralization- the lack of entralrd 
5. interdependence 

These five factors structure the online world. Hence they structure the opportunities for crime and the ways that people commit crimes and breach network security. 


New crimes in the digital networked env. Anonymity, interconnectedness, and accessibility to vast amounts off info facilitate older crimes and set the stage for new one, including pure info crimes.  Long the activities that gov now see to prevent are third party misappropriation fo trade secrets over the internet, economic espionage, unauthorized access to encrhteds  eee





Emergence of a new type of organized criminal groups that operate only in cyberspace: 
Cybercrime is has transformed from separate acts committed by individuals to sophisticated and professional activity as part of professional networks as long-term sustainable operations. 

the past decade, cybercrime has gone through a transformationprocess from fragmented acts committed by individualsto increasingly sophisticated and highly professionalized activity.Moreover, cybercrime is believed to be at the stage ofa fast expanding illegal industry where criminal activities areconducted by professional networks as long-term sustainableoperations. Due to the newness of the phenomenon, there isstill a considerable lack of research on how these networks incyberspace are structured and how they operate. However, itis currently under discussion that we are witnessing the emergenceof a new type of organised criminal groups that operatessolely in cyberspace: groups that have not yet been consolidatedinto a stable system but are dangerous nonetheless.


The digital age has given rise to a new type of organized criminal groups that operate only in cyberspace. This is the transformation of cybercrime into a gloabal, 
illegal industry with a new type of organized criminal groups thriving behind it. 
What is the structure of online criminal groups and how do they function. t

Initially, the cybercrime scene was dominated by young hackers  accessing computer systems and breaking security measures mainly for fun. With the development 
of the digital economy, both the criminal landscape and the motivation of offenders have 
changed dramatically. High rewards combined with low risks have made digital networks an 
attractive environment for carious types of profit driven criminals thriving on cybercrime.
